RATING: 7
Good game but nothing revolutionnary. Important to check what other people do especially when they try to end the game. It is more a "race" game than a connection game. You have to decide quickly if you go with big bonus (Baiern or anything but bairn) or if you go with a bigger Coach. The inclusion of the Support role is good as each support action fulfill different needs.

Feel a bit dry and underwhelming to me though.

Update: Played again. This game is really a race. You cannot influence your opponent. You just have to be quicker than them. I won easily by never losing a turn and never building a road too long or too short. I earn all my carts in the order. I still think the game is a bit bland.

Update: the game is well constructed. There is a different action for each "goal" in game: drawng more cards, plagin more cards and getting a carriage. I still think there is no real player interaction except for the race aspect of getting bonuses. All in all it's a well crafted game but I think the "fun" is missing from it. There is no real tension (like in Ticket to ride to which it is often compared).

RATING: 7
A simple set collection game where you are trying to build postal routes and when you score your route, it allows you to put post offices on different color terrain.  Once you have a post office in all the terrain, you collect a scoring tile for the region.  It has a Ticket to Ride complexity so it is very light, family weight game.  Some people find the game a little dry, but I like it.  It is very good Spiel des Jahres winner.  The expansions open the game up with other ways to play and more maps.

RATING: 6
It's hard to shake Ticket to Ride instincts when playing this, given that TtR is in this game's DNA, but it's quite different.

I like the race aspect, the push-your-luck element, and the way the bonuses are structured. With two, it's a bit more strategic; with 3+ it's more tactical since you have a reduced chance of getting what you're planning for.

The board is beautiful and pleasant-looking, if a bit subtle; I'd prefer slightly clearer borders and a bit more differentiation between the cities.

RATING: 7
March 2013: I'm not sure if I enjoy this or Ticket to Ride better. I've rated them both the same.

Update 1/2/14: I hadn't played this one in a while. I had an itch to play it tonight. I'm going to leave my rating where it's at after 2 more plays. It's a cute game. There's definitely nothing groundbreaking here--just a quick family game. It could easily frustrate serious gamers because of the high amount of randomness. Even in a 2 player game, the change in card setup can become chaotic, leading to turn-based rather than long-term strategical planning. That said, the game does offer some alternative paths to victory if you are unfortunate with your card drawing. I think this is a great family game, especially if you have kids from 8-14. In short, it might sit on the shelf for a while.

RATING: 7
GAMEPLAY: A network-building and card-drafting eurogame. Each turn, players draw one or two city cards from a display of six face-up cards or from the face-down deck. Players play one or two cards from their hand during each turn to begin or add to a route consisting of adjacent cities; routes that include three or more cities may be closed and scored. Upon closing and scoring a route a player may place houses in the cities included in the route, earn bonus tiles, and obtain successively larger carriages, all of which increase the player‚Äôs victory points. The game ends at the end of a round in which one or more players either exhaust their supply of 20 houses or earn the largest available carriage.

WEIGHT: Medium-light. The rules are not complex.

PLAYER INTERACTION/CONFLICT: Low. Any number of players may place a house in the same city.

PLAYER COUNT: Scales very well from two to four players. Gameplay feels the same at all player counts. An excellent two-player game.

LUCK: Low to moderate. It‚Äôs a card game and sometimes you are looking for a particular card. But the display of six cards decreases the problem. Players also have the option of resetting the display of six cards.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Nearly perfect light-medium euro. Simple rules, legitimate decisions to be made each turn (but not too heavy to overwhelm), light player interaction (but not in a nasty way), a feeling of a race with multiple ways to win, and beautiful artwork (subdued color scheme is soothing rather than drab, in this case).

I really like that you can close the game out with the 7 town carriage or by getting all your houses out. It is definitely possible to win with a series of short routes if you get all your houses out each time and get a bunch of the region bonuses, especially if your opponents still have many houses in hand.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.1
Nice components, rules are not too difficult to explain, yet the game doesn't taste too simple to general gamers. So it has all the elements to be entitled as a "great gateway game". However, There are some minor but obvious problems in here. The rule sounds strange when it is applied to a "postal system". For example, it is not intuitive to have a rule like "put only one office into each different region of the route, or put all office into only one region of the route". And the color tone of the board is dull, tho the artwork is fine. 
-----Update: after 4 online 2players games, I agree that it could be a good couple game that can also scale up. It is still painful to look for the places on the map before I remember all city name.
-----Update: The more I played it the more I appreciate it. Raised to 9.

RATING: 9
When this was released I heard it compared often to Ticket to Ride. There a many similarities between the games but also some significant differences:

- There is less direct interaction and conflict between players. It's a friendlier game than Ticket to Ride (which can get quite cut-throat).
- It's even more of a race than Ticket to Ride. The strategy of hoarding cards can work in Ticket to Ride, but won't work here.
- The choice of special role each round in Thurn und Taxis is delicious. You often want to do 3 or 4 but can only choose one.

I enjoy both, but I think my preference is for Thurn und Taxis.

RATING: 7.5
Strangely, the first word that pops to my mind about this game is - mature (not in that sense, you rascal! ;) ).

It has very subtle yet truly masterful artwork. It has an accurate map of a portion of historical Europe, and its theme portrays accurate historical developments. Mechanics are simple and enjoyable. Components are nothing flashy, but pretty and top quality, and with nice details which show on a deeper inspection.

All in all, a very nice game. No big enthusiasm, no big complaints, nice, subtle, and... well, mature.

RATING: 5.5
Simple route builder but quite fun. Without blocking it's less interactive than Ticket to Ride and without route cards it's less directed. It's all about chasing bonuses and optimizing them based on card availability.

After quite a few more plays, I'm beginning to feel the endgame is too swingy. Equal-ish players with equal-ish luck can be neck-and-neck until one hits the final play, ends the game, and wins by a margin. I know that doesn't read well, but it might be killing the replayability of this game for me. But that was after ~30 plays, so....

I've definitely reached the point where I will never request this game again. I got a solid 30 plays out of it, and I'd play casually with others by request, but I'm basically finished with it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Players build routes through multiple cities by playing cards for each city; players get points for building longer routes, and near the end of the game must build long routes to get points.  While which city-cards are available adds luck to the gameplay, the game is very strategic/tactical as the scoring options allow for multiple methods to get points (building a long road, getting houses in each color, getting all the houses of one color, etc.), each of which takes planning and responsiveness to achieve.  There is no resource production, trading, auctions, or even currency in the game.  The one problem I can forsee is that near the end the game can devolve into a card-hunting game (wherein each player needs one card to win).

RATING: 8
I bought this originally on account of it being an SdJ winner.  I was new to the hobby and this was one of my first purchases that I made without knowing anything about it, but based on the award alone, and the fact that I really enjoyed Ticket to Ride, Settlers, and Carcassonne, also SdJ winners.  I was immediately underwhelmed when I got a chance to play.  Rating - 6.

It wasn't until a little while later when I played a 2-player game, and playing in online games, where I began to appreciate it more.  It was a tight little game.  Not genius, but pleasant, and with the feeling of a race to see who can most quickly raise up their carriage cards or place their post offices, since this is usually a good indication (but not surety) of the leader.  Now I'm glad that I kept it around since it fits nicely into its SdJ category -- a quick, lighter game for family and friends. Rating - 8. 

The expansion board of Power & Glory adds some more variety and flavor.  Most of the smaller expansions I could take or leave.  I don't think they add that much strategy.

RATING: 8
Thurn and Taxis has some very unique elements but does have a similar feel to other card drafting (set collection) games such as Ticket to Ride, Web of Power (aka China), Hacienda, and even Showmanager.  It is fairly light on strategy (which is why it appealed to the German Game of the Year voters), but offers enough agonizing decisions to keep things interesting.   Other than hoarding cards someone else needs, there is little you can do to slow down the leader.   Some might call it multi-player solitaire.  But that doesn't bother me, as I tend to enjoy many of those type of games (Princes of Florence being my favorite multi-player solitaire type of game).

RATING: 7
Theme is nicely woven into the game and the game play is tight.  Beautifully crafted artwork and components.  The concept is very easy to learn but the degree of strategy is enough to keep the synapses firing without becoming too overwhelming.  

Due to its rather quick play time, it can serve as a nice filler game after a grueling epic when you are looking to take it easy but still want a challenge.  Your actions have enough of an impact on other players to promote a healthy degree of interaction, but not too much to immerse you in politics or bantering.  So its a good way to strike a balance if coming out of a more competitive gaming session without swinging too far into the dry worker placement/resource management arena.

It's also a good game whether you play 2 players or four players.  In all, very well designed and executed.  Something I will always be happy to play and happy to own.

RATING: 9
Good Light/Medium weight set collection, route building game.  About the same complexity as Carcassonne/Ticket to Ride, but allows for more long term strategy, as the goals are completely determined by the player (getting long routes, all colors bonus, gray area, etc.) and not by a card draw. RATING: 5
Moderately enjoyable game with nice graphics. I think its less accessible to non-gamers than TtR but probably a good transition from there towards more complex gaming. The game play is mostly tactical and a bit dull as it's mainly just waiting for the appearance of that critical card you need to complete a route. Player interaction is pretty much limited to the "Administrator" role, hence the frequent use of the apt metaphor "multiplayer solitaire" by other BGGers to describe T&T. 

The amount of times I've played this game is no reflection of how much I enjoy it. It just seems the be a game that is usually available and the lowest common denominator after everyone decides on what not to play. In fact, T&T is probably the personification of why dull Eurogames do so well among anonymous gamers - you just play "among" (ie solitaire) other gamers with an inoffensive ruleset without risking (and failing) on any real personal interaction with other people.

Small note: I have seen one session of this game go for 3 hours! A small preview of hell!

RATING: 7
Everybody seems to compare it to Ticket To Ride, but I think the comparison only holds up for the card draw mechanism, and even that is not exactly the same.  The theme is maybe a bit similar, but for the rest, the way you place your branches, and more importantly how you score requires much more attention. RATING: 6.5
A decent game... certainly reminiscent of Ticket To Ride. Limited experience with this so far but I can't help but call this a slightly more thoughtful but solitary version of TtR. In TtR you have tickets basically mandating where you need to place your trains... and you need to deal with others getting in your way and come up with plan B and C quite often. In Thurn & Taxis you can basically set a plan in action according to your cards and yes you have the other players swooping in to pick up the bonus chits before you can reach them but all in all it's like a race where everyone is doing their own thing and the interaction level doesn't feel quite as strong as in TtR. The blocking action in Thurn & Taxis is also not really a factor. Both games have luck of the draw issues and that can likely be mitigated a bit more in T&T which is why I think it's the slightly more "advanced" game. I don't know if it's quite as interesting or fun as TtR though which in the end is what makes or breaks a game. For now I'm giving this a 6.5 and hopefully with more plays this may rise up above that level but I still think TtR is the better bang in this particular genre. I must say I can't really see why this game would win SdJ after seeing how similar in concept it is to TtR yet lacks the overall spark of that game. Oh well... to each their own.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Themed after the 19th century German postal system, one attempts to establish postal houses in all areas of Germany. A player drafts cards into their hand, plays them down to form a route, then play down postal houses on the route, either all in one province, or one in each of the provinces. Being able to form postal houses in all provinces, or all in one province earns VP chits for that player, and VPs decrease for the next player. One also earns VPs for the length of their routes. It is a race to finish, and players can use one of 4 special abilities per turn to aid them. It's a fun game. The mechanics are not new, but they are blended together to form a good game.

RATING: 8
I enjoy this quite a bit. It feels like a cross between TtR and Funkenschlag, a bit more strategic than TTR and less luck-prone, but still a good family game that plays under an hour and is extremely easy to explain. There might not be an abundance of interactive elements in the game, but sucess does require a player to keep a close eye on the point scoring by the other players, and an ability to make some tactical changes based on that. For me the game does not fulfill the criteria of multiplayer solitaire. The map is a bit fuzzy and the road system should be more clearly marked, now diluted by the cities.

Impression after 1 play - a decent game, but I wouldn't say it's great. Definitely feels like a mixture of T2R and Web of Power, but I think I prefer Web of Power because it allows a little bit more flexibility to players(cards depicting regions instead of each city). That said, you-have-to-pay-attention-to-others-kind of player interaction is usually not thrilling enough to me. Guess I am too lazy to do that.

RATING: 5
I prefer heavy games, but this is my preferred "light" game so far. Much better than other more appreciated "light" games here on BGG (surely better than Ticket to Ride, just to make an example). Even better than Carcassone, the game that I used to propose to non gamers. Even heavy gamers can like it, since there are many different paths to victory and it is possible to have your own personal path to victory. There is luck, but less decisive than some critiques let intend (I think at least 90 % of the games the strongest player wins). I don't agree that it seems a multi player solitaire and that there is no interaction at all. The key point of the game is timing and a player can decide the length of the game in many different ways... so the timing itself is the interaction, and it is not a small one, IMHO.

UPDATE January 2009
I like the game less lately. And, even without considering the heavy games that I prefer, there are better light games that appeared lately which I would prefer to play (i.e. Dominion, Giants, Steel Driver).

UPDATE
After the appearance of Hansa Teutonica I think it is very unlikely that I will play this game again. So rating further decreased.

UPDATE March 2013
After the appearance of games like Terra Mystica or The Great Zimbabwe my wish to play this game is further decreased.

RATING: 8

It's not the right choice if cutthroat playing is wished - but an ideal family game.

RATING: 7.4
At my first games I impressed from this game's simplicity and fun and give it 7.8 points. However I decreased its point from 7.8 to 7.5 after losing several games aganist my brother Orcun and friend Serhan (I generally beat them in other games) because of high luck effect on last games. I cannot even make my strategy well because I cannot predict which cards will show up next. I make a strategy but the card I need do not show up even I make administrator and change all cards. So you do not have to take risk in that game but you cannot make high scores without taking risks if you have not started game well. Game start is also effected by luck. Generally it is a well designed good and fun game with high replayibility but it has less and luck-effected strategy so I give it a 7.5

RATING: 8
All this said, it is a very light game and there is a lot of luck. I would find it difficult to say you can become a pro at Thurn, since you have to hope your cards come out and if they don%u2019t well, it will cost you wasted turns. Also, some might be frustrated that the decisions they make have little effect on the other players and that the game seems like a race with too much luck. I cannot really argue with that, but for a light simple game, everyone I played with enjoyed it. Sometimes it is just nice to play something that does not cause too much brain drain, yet still involves enough strategy to prevent it from being simply a %u201Clucky player wins all the time%u201D type of game. This is a nice family game that can be enjoyed by hard core players as well, but I would not necessarily recommend it to those who only like pure strategy games and mock any aspect of luck. All in all, a nice addition to my collection.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This gets compared to Ticket to Ride more than it should.  It shares the card drafting aspect somewhat, but the card play itself is quite different.  Hand management in this game is much trickier, but the tension of getting blocked is replaced by a race type tension.  Thurn and Taxis can be described as a hand management puzzle race whereas Ticket to Ride has a much stronger element of keeping your opponents from completing their goals while you advance yours, though Thurn and Taxis has some of this as well.  Though Ticket to Ride is vastly more popular, both games have aged extremely well.

RATING: 7
I've played this game at a local board game meetup. I feel the cards are pretty balanced to have 3 cards for each city in the deck. I was fearing that I'd not be able to build any more routes and thus has to discard my present tableau without being able to score. Luckily, it didn't happen in the game that I played. 
The end game condition also makes it an interesting game. I have a feeling that rushing the carriages won't help me and it didn't because I didn't have enough bonus tiles to compete for the end game.
I don't really feel like there is too much of a player interaction there. I know you can wipe the board to hurt a player, but you don't know if it will either.

Another turn off for me is the Cities name are all foreign to me but I am sure repeated plays will make it easier. It is color coded so that makes it a bit easier to manage.

It's a good game, but I don't know if I will own one or not.

RATING: 8
A fun game in the vein of Ticket to Ride but far less luck-driven.  The card draws provide a bit of luck, and an occasional clearing of the cards provides some chaos.  There is a healthy amount of player interaction, but it's long-term rather than short-term, as each player races to end the game or to grab chips before the others.  It seems that multiple plays provide more strategic and tactical insight, but I anticipate that multiple plays may bore me.  This evaluation and rating is based on one play, and I would enjoy playing it again, though I may burn out after 5 or so plays.

RATING: 6
Playing the base game often online has now cemented my impression: it is like a jigsaw puzzle (with beautiful map art) which is ideally (i.e. efficiently) made from 5 pieces of increasing sizes (3,4,5,6 and 7 spots) but with the little wrinkle being there will be at least 2 spots missing from the puzzle.

The wrinkle doesn't bother me, the almost restrictive reward of putting down the pieces in size order starts to (you can build say 5 then 5 size etc but only get points for a 3 and 4 size).

The puzzlement continues with the strange and counterintuitive placement on the spots which causes the piece you are putting down to morph or flip flop from one formation to another, your choice influenced by how much vp you will get when you claim certain spots. Admittedly this is the interesting part of the game....

The pieces are made of strings of connected routes, players interacting by weaving the same routes so the race is for finishing quickly as there is a vp countdown in value for different regions on the board.(Exciting stuff). 

But now comes the bad vibe part: sometimes there is a relationship test when you may blatantly taking 1 or 2 cards or scrap the display that would cap an end part of your opponents route. This may have a knock-on effect on your opponent which may cause all the hard decision work of building the route to be dismantled if they can't find on their turn the same or alternative card. I feel the route won't be the only thing that will break down.....

It is this restrictive building of the routes which can make or break the game. Like I said earlier it is like building a jigsaw where doing it in size sequencing made reap better rewards, but at times it is like wearing a straitjacket too, not a challenge I enjoy and can really only play with the Messenger expansion as it loosens the buckles a bit and provides some hope.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
-

Finally a game by Seyfarth. Decent enough lighter game and nothing in the Puerto Rico class. You create routes from one city to another, passing throug a variable number of cities. All of your victory ponts come from the length of routes you make and how fast you get to visit all the cities in a regions. There is a mechanic here similar to Ticket to Ride: Marklin, where the earlier arrivals to certain regions get to pick up higher-numbered victroy point tokens. 

Some strategies and tension since it is a race game after all, but there are lots of chaos and luck of the draw. Overall a light game to play once in a while.
[Rated: 07/23/06]

RATING: 7
A quick playing and simple route building game. In this game you draw cards and place them in front of you so that they reflect a chain of towns on the board. Then, when you feel good about your chain, you score it and place houses in one of two patterns depending on your strategy. There are also those Feldian point bonuses for the first player to score a length or complete area, where the first player to do the thing gets the highest value chip at the top of the pile. Very cute, but the dry graphic design kept this from the table, and other games overshadow it in it's slot. 
:nostar: Art and components
:star: Innovative mechanics
:nostar: Handles 5 or more players
:star: Good with min or max players
:star: Low time between turns
:star: Comfortable complexity
:star: Re-playability
:star::star::nostar: Enjoyment

RATING: 8
A superior game of about the complexity of Hansa. It has a bit of TtR flavor in the card drawing and placement. Both strategy (optimizing the bonus tiles) and luck (draw of the cards) are well balanced. Except for poaching a card needed by another player (which isn't a good plan unless you need that card, thereby it is no longer poaching...) there is no opportunity for screwage. There is a race to score the various bonus tiles as early as possible though. Better be prepared to get the 7 carriage on the last turn. Use of the Cartwright special option is essential to this task (as others will be using it). Work in 'radial' lines, from the outer areas into Baiern, to acquire the bonus chips while placing houses in the multiple provice mode. Filling in Baiern first is a loser.

RATING: 7

There are bonus points by completing whole colors.

Have you ever wished you could build a postal empire in renaissance Germany? [i]Well now you can![/i] In Thurn and Taxis you will be doing that very thing! Now, the theme isn't exactly fascinating, but the game play is. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
When we first got this game, I was bit skeptical about it because while researching Govind came across sentences such as ,"This is another TTR". Because of this, I was under the impression that it is going to be a gateway game and I might not enjoy it. While we were unboxing the game, I found some cards to be similar to those of Trambahn which is one game I absolutely can not stand. So all in all, I had very low expectations from the game. 
However, after playing the game, I was never more happy to be proven wrong. This game is a gem and I am surprised how many people don't talk about it. 

Reasons I love the game:
1) Building a network of post offices through connecting routes give me a hands on feeling of being involved. I find it very thematic and engaging.
2) 4 special abilities make sure that there is always extra to be done in your turn. It is not a simple 'take a card, play a card' mechanic.
3) Although gameplay is very simple, the game has considerable depth. Just to plan and get the best possible route while installing as many post offices as possible is pretty deep.
4) Healthy competition. The game fosters healthy competition where you are competing with other player to get area bonus and multiple other bonus. At the same time, you never intentionally hurt your opponent.
5) Art and component quality. Classy artwork accompanied by good quality components. Linen finish on the cards make gameplay experience super awesome.
6) Germany's early modern map make it really fun to try and read the names aloud. And as a history buff, the theme appeals to me on a personal level.

All in all, an awesome game which Govind and I can play again and again.

RATING: 9
Players: 2-4, best with any; 60 min; Weight: 2.26
Wonderful, well designed game.  Kind of a mixture of Ticket to Ride & Castles of Burgundy.

Postal route building game with a race element, as the first player to complete an objective will always gain the most victory points. Intelligent use of a limited "enhancement" each turn -- to gain an extra card, play an extra card, replace cards, etc. -- is key in winning. Once a strategy is pursued, aggressive opponents can thwart you at the cost of delaying their own strategy, as with Ticket to Ride, or you could simply be blocked by the right cards not being drawn.

RATING: 7.5
Good game.  My biggest gripe is if a mistake is made, the only way you can catch up is if the people ahead makes a mistake as well.

8-12-11 Update: Actually beginning to not find this game fun at all.  Even while looking at my opponents route and occasionally taking a card she needed, it just isn't all that fun.  There just isn't much interaction and it really feels like solitaire.  Not what I'm looking for in a two player game.

8-26-12 Update:  Found out we've been scoring this game all wrong.  You only score your largest carriage not all of them and you subtract the number of posts you have left.  Guess this is what you get when you rely on someone to teach you the game and don't read the rules for yourself...its become a fun game again.

RATING: 7.5
Thurn and Taxis is an area control game with route building via a card drafting mechanic.  No two games play the same, and there is more than one strategy that will secure enough victory points to win the game.  On their turn players add at least one card to their hand representing cities on the board.  They then must play one card representing a route.  They may only play a card they do not have in their route, and the card must be adjacent to one of the cities on the two endpoints of their route.  Players may then score their route which allows them to place houses in cities (from their route) either one in each of the regions in your route, or all of the cities in one region in your route.

Victory points are awarded for routes 5 or more cities in length, and for have houses in all cities of a given region.  The first person to do this gets more points than the rest, and eventually it's not worth anything.  At the end of the game any unplaced houses count against you, so the players need to balance the pace of the game and try not to let it end while they have a deficit of points.

The tension in the game comes from trying to be first to capture points, but also maintaining your route, because if you cannot add to your route you lose it.  All decisions in the game are strategic but not unforgiving of mistakes.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
This is one of my favorite game night ender games.  There's some thought involved, but it also can be viewed as a nice light solitaire game.

It supports varied strategies to win, and does require the ability to pay attention to what everyone else is doing to play it well, however it still plays OK for those people who don't pay attention on anyone else's turn -- and still plays fairly quickly.

With only small amounts of downtime, and the ability to play the game without paying attention to anyone else puts it, for me, as a stepping stone game.

A stepping stone game is one that is played after the gateway game, but before tackling some of the more complex games in our hobby.  A good one to teach after they've learned ticket to ride, or catan.

RATING: 6
Approx weight: 1020 grams
Not too heavy game that moves along at a decent pace and manages to play differently with each outing. At first you think there's not a lot of player interaction, until with subsequent playings you start to see the possibilities of jumping in before the others and claiming the higher victory point markers and occasionally claiming a city card just for blocking purposes. Just try grabbing all the Lodz city cards and see how the other players feel about it!
The game is fun with 2-4 players, although the competition is more fierce with four players competing for the four city cards in the deck - tends to lead to more card cycling actions being used to get the desired card.
If you're looking for a game easy on the rules, that's fun and with a fairly low level of meanness, then I can highly recommend this one.

RATING: 8
At first glance, it looks similar to Ticket to Ride, until you play.  This game truly feels like a race as players, who represent postal companies in 18th century Germany, race to get their post offices and psotal routes established.  The unique mechanic of using the map of the game board as the rules of how one can play their cards, added to the fact one can break one rule per turn, make this a wonderful game.  The twist is that the fastest doesn't always mean first; players need to move slow enough to try and build as many post offices as possible, even if it means shorter routes, since VPs are subtracted for unbuilt offices.

This seems lighter than it actually is -- perhaps because of the quick turns.  Strong game.  

[COLOR=#006600][b]Why we own it: [/b][/COLOR] 

It's becoming one of my "go to" games.  The rules are easy to remember (even after long gaps between sessions), while the depth is satisfying.  And the several expansions promise continued interest.

RATING: 1.5
TTR reworked as a MPS euro puzzle. Should be fine for those who like Alhambra. 

Route building is interesting, but with the scoring and whatnot there's so many things too juggle you won't look at what other players are doing. At all. Just what level of coach they have and that's it. Like BMC, this is a race, but closer to those of euro puzzle engines (it's not an engine, BUT your set collecting is pretty much tied to an excel spread sheet designer made up). And with all juggling that consumes your mind, it's hard to say it's ever rewarding or justified. I don't dislike it, I think the route building is a nice mechanic/feature which makes thematic sense, Bavaria is a good place to travel across by mind and as far as euro puzzles go at least it's not one of changing resources into other resources. 

Played this a few times too many with eurogamers and lost my taste for brown pastels and silent optimising.

RATING: 7.5
Players draft and play 1-2 cards each turn to link cities. There are multiple ways of scoring linked cities (do you place a house in one city in each linked region or place a house in all cities in a single region). Hand management is crucial as players HAVE to draw AND place a route card each turn. If you're overly ambitious, you might have to end up discarding the ENTIRE route you've built so far. DOH. The pace of the game is driven by the players and one must be careful to keep up with the pack. Several potential flaws have been mentioned: it feels little solitaire-ish (but so's TTR) and it can drag if several players start taking too long calculating all the potential routes in their head. I think the sweet spot is 3 players.

UPDATE: A friend described this as Ticket to Ride without the 'meanness' of blocking people. I agree. Seyfarth has taken the TtR drafting of cards and given his spin on the game. There are no secret destinations: replaced by common pool of VP points for achieving goals first. Like TTR Marklin, there is a need to drop off your house early enough to get the higher point VP tokens. Also, one must learn to manage your hand (you're forced to discard down to 3 cards after completing routes) and plan several moves ahead.

RATING: 4.5
T&T is a lovely game, and it's an extremely clean system which nicely utilizes proven mechanisms. I feel as if I should really like it. But there's also almost zero player interaction, almost zero tension, almost zero excitement. It's one of those games, like TtR (to which it is frequently compared), in which players attempt to complete routes. Completing routes gets you little victory point bonuses, and your goal is to get as many of those bonuses as possible while trying to ensure that the game ends when you are in an ascendent position. The rules are elegant, but I just find the game ho-hum. There is nothing especially satisfying about playing it, although I'm happy to play it while carrying on a conversation. I tend to dislike "multiplayer solitaire" games in which you try to build something, and in which other players can only thwart your efforts in passive-aggressive ways - which describes T&T pretty well. The only way to mess with another player is to pick up cards you "think" she might want. This is the only real interaction in the game, and it's pretty weak - but I simply don't care for this sort of interaction. If there is a conflict of interests in a game, I like it to be more direct. In Tikal, you can take control (for scoring purposes) of someone else's ruins. In Lost Valley, you can obtain gold from a mine another player spent valuable resources to build. In Puerto Rico, you can take a role card desired by someone else - but it has a *major* impact on their plans. In T&T, taking a card someone else wants (if you guess correctly about that) is like pinching them, not knocking them out with a knuckle sandwich. My complaint does not arise from lack of appreciation for subtlety. I love subtlety, but let there be some deviousness, for crying out loud. I've meditated a bit on this game, and I think although I find the presentation beautiful, it just doesn't feel that much like a game to me. More of an activity. Even in Lord of the Rings, a cooperative game, there is a strong feeling of competition - against the Sauron-Knizia evil mastermind, aka The Game.

RATING: 3
Boring multiplayer solitaire without blocking and almost no player interaction. The routes you can build are dictated by the faceup city cards, so there are almost no meaningful decisions to be made. To complete a route you have to wait for the right city to show up, so there is a lot of luck involved. A 2-player game is a runaway leader race for the big point chits.

Thurn & Taxis is a good example that the "Spiel des Jahres" award doesn't mean anything. Ticket to Ride, which obviously "inspired" this game, is much better.

RATING: 4.5
We Await Silent Tristero's Empire.

This is a decent little puzzle, with about zero interaction.  Nothing really new here, but it is relaxing and familiar so I wouldn't protest to playing it.  People compare it to Ticket to Ride, but that is only because it also uses the Venture card drafting system.  This is all about hand management, there are many options available to you, but it is easy to get boned by bad card draws if you aren't careful.  Planners should like the game, but those that want to play something with any direct conflict, competition or even a way to effect other players should look elsewhere. 

If I were to say it was close to any other game I would put this more in the lines of St. Petersburg, all solitaire card drafting but without the money. Also both games use the I'll take the card you want "mechanic" to give at least some illusion of interactivity, although the game is so tactical (especially with the card sweep deal) that you can't rely on cards coming to you anyway.  I certainly like this game more, but it seems much less of a game.

For pure card drafting games like this, they will always inevitably be compared to Showmanager/Atlantic Star by me.  By that comparison, it just doesn't cut the mustard.

Totally inoffensive.  Somewhat compelling online, but best played as a diversion if at all.

RATING: 8.5
This game is somewhat hard to rate - it's not as deep as some of the more strategic games (ie Puerto Rico, Princes of Florence), and it doesn't have the obvious interaction of some of the lighter games (ie Settlers of Catan).  However, once you delve into the game, it becomes readily apparent that there is a good level of strategic/tactical depth that easily overrides the luck of the draw factor this game has.  Also, while people claim you can play this game like solitaire, if you want to win against good players, you need to keep track of what they are doing, and sometimes more importantly, the pace they are employing.  As many have mentioned, there may seem to be a question mark over the replayability of the game, but I think the luck of the draw factor and multiple paths to victory makes this game viable over a long period of time.

RATING: 8

Still an '8' and were there an 'off-track betting' facility that handicapped choices for the Spiele de Jahre, I'd be laying money down on this one for 2006.

RATING: 7
T&T works well enough as an entry-level German family game.  SdJ?  Whatever.  Every turn, you draw one or two city cards, then play one or two in front of you to make a route.  When you're satisfied with that route (usually after building on it for several successive turns) you evaluate (score and clear) the route for the opportunity to place markers on the board and score some points.  You're limited by 4 things: 1) you can only work on one route at a time; 2)you must place at least one card onto your route per turn; 3)hand size limit is 3; and 4)the available cards.  

Basically this game comes down to a race between you and whichever other player is employing the exact same strategy as you.  It's a game of objectives--to be first to place a marker into every country --to be first to place a marker in every city in a country--to be first to build a 5, 6, or 7 city route, etc.  Because there's no limit to the number of players' markers in a city, there is no blocking strategy.  So it's truly you against the card display.  There are decisions to be made, but to call it strategic or tactical is rather grandiose.  TtR-Europe and Marklin both offer much more tension and interaction than this title.

All that said, it comes with a beautifully illustrated board and quality components, and I would definitely play it again as a change of pace game.

RATING: 6.5
Like Web of Power, in that you draw cards from a face-up display and play them to place houses. But you can't place the houses willy nilly - must add to either end of a chain you are building. You build chains (routes) of different lengths. Points come from finishing routes (longer = more), finishing routes sooner (more pts than later), and for having houses throughout each region or in all regions (again, more pts for those who accomplish these sooner). 

After initial plays: OK, but not terribly exciting. 6

After (Sep-2010) a few more plays on yucata, 2er: hmm, this may be better than I thought (at least 2er); you have more control, and the game should play fairly quickly (appropriate for its weight). 6.5?

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
To anyone who has played Ticket to Ride this game is going to look familiar.  This is a route building game where players draft cards into their hand from a display or face-down deck and play these cards to build routes from location to location.

The goals in this game are a little different though.  Instead of having specific routes to complete for points there are specific goal tokens that deal with getting pieces in all the locations in certain areas and length of route.  Players decide on their own when to complete a route and when a route is completed pieces are placed in either each location in that route in one area or one piece in each area that has a location as part of that route.

The thing that makes this game so variable is the use of the different officials.  During a turn a player can use only one but there are 4 different ones that have different benefits in different phases.

The game is incredibly accessible and looks nice with a nice insert which is also nice.  It does have a lot of similarities to Ticket to Ride but also has its own identity.  There are a good amount of decisions to make and I quite enjoyed playing it.

RATING: 6
Enjoyable, quick and easy route planner. You build routes via stage coaches in Southern Germany. The scoring is actually done in a refreshing clever way. Speed is key as I realized, and that's what I like so much about "Thurn and Taxis", it is best played fast, and without any extra squiggles and therefor doesn't outlast its welcome. RATING: 9
A fine game of connections and racing to make bonuses for them.  From a display of six city cards (or the top of the deck) you draw one or two cards each turn, add one or two to your route, and score for it if you're ready to score.  The fact that you *must* add at least one city to your route each turn or lose the whole route gives the game an enjoyable planning element.  P.S.  Raising this after 3 years of enjoyment from 8 to 9 because it is just so darned interestingly replayable for every number of players from 2 to 4.  This has been a games night staple since it came out and I am still jazzed about it every time I get the chance to play it.

RATING: 8
Played 10+ times. Very intriguing. It's pretty light, but I'm interested in exploring the mechanics.  My first impression is that it's a race game; for the bonuses, you always get 1 more point for doing something first and for the carriages, you end the game.  I don't know if the game will ever end by someone playing their 20 houses on the 22 spaces. Great for the work crowd at lunch. ***UPDATE** There's definitely more than one way to skin the cat.  It's definitely easier to finish the carriages than the houses but the houses are possible (I played 19 in one game).  At first glance the start player appears to have an advantage because he can get everything just before everyone else for one additional point.  But on the board play this is relegated because you definitely don't have to go for the same bonuses as everyone else.  If everything else is equal and everyone goes for the 3,4,5,6 and 7 carriages in order at the same speed the advantage will come from getting the 5, 6 and 7 length route bonuses first.  My suggestion don't just blindly follow the first player; Do a 7 instead of your 6 to pull that bonus first; pull the Cartwright to end the game earlier.  In reality all things are not equal and everyone is in control of the end game.  In the mechanics of the endgame the advantage is definitely for the last player.  Once he's done no one else gets an additional turn and every half finished route doesn't score anything.  The first player  has to be vary wary of other players finishing with 5 or 6 plus Cartwright and possibly jump ship in anticipation with a shorter route.  There's much risk involved in that because then the other player can wait an additional turn to get a longer route, while you can't do anything.  See also my discussion of the length of the game here. http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/117660 2006/08/06

RATING: 6
There is a bit of everything in this simple game. You connect cities. Score points for long chains. You try to have one city in territory of each color or try to have your post offices in each city of the territory of same color. You collect cards and tokens. Everything sounds like a great game. But it lucks something. Game has no interaction at all. It plays more like a solitare then a addictive board game. I can easily see it played by 1 person only. It is not a much difference to play it with more players. But we love to play board games with friends and challenge them a bit. This game offers no chellenge at all. Board is very nice, machanics work well but game is boring and repetitive after few plays. I say no to solitare games! But i guess it might be fun for some also as a gateway game.

RATING: 6
This rating could climb higher. It's very good game for patient card players who like quiet and reflective types of games. Unlike other games based on drawing cards to make a connective path, such as ticket to ride and china, here you dont really block anyone. So it's sort of solitaire but do interact with others by how you manipulate the deck, what you draw. This takes a little more patience and memory than directly attacking people. On the downside there are probably lots of card games that play faster (we did four player in about an hour, but might be faster). Also the scoring system does not thrill me. It is not overwrought but still with about 5 separate ways to score, it's close. Such systems detract from a classic feel.

RATING: 7.2
tl;dr: very good

This game has been around for over a decade now! I'm getting old!
Of course this is not my initial reaction, I did play this game a good amount when it came out. I owned a copy, but sold it after I felt I was done with it. But I hadn't played it quite a while, so this is my impression after playing it again recently.
This game has aged quite well. It falls into the family strategy category as the rules are pretty simple and accessible, but there certainly is a very solid amount of strategy there. There is some luck in what cards come out of course, but there's ways to deal with that and it usually evens out over the length of the game.
This is certainly a game like you would expect from Hans in Gl√ºck: it is very, very well developed. It is very clean without loosing depth.
All in all this is a very solid offering that doesn't feel dated at all yet. Certainly worth playing.

RATING: 7

I know there are some people that say that when playing with, for example, spouses, they try not to block in TtR.  Thurn and Taxis may scratch the same itch yet prevent the hard feelings, while not forcing players to play sub-optimally.

RATING: 8
A unique design by Seyfarth and Seyfarth. This quickly became one of my wife's favorites. The game has low confrontation, allowing you to essentially work on your own position while you race for the best VP tokens. Building of the continuous routes is a neat mechanic, as well as the two placement options when you complete a route.

I don't find this game to be like anything else I've played. I'm not sure why it gets compared to Ticket to Ride, other than the word "routes". For what it's worth, I prefer this game to TTR. I find the decisions to be more meaningful. While there is some randomness in the game, it is not present to the extreme seen in TTR.

This game scales very well. Any number of players is fun.

RATING: 6
In Thurn & Taxis, players build post office routes across Bavaria and the regions around, collecting bonus points in various ways. The board shows a map of all the towns, with roads leading from each one to some of its neighbors. There are various colored regions around the board, most with one or two towns, and a large region with all the Bavarian towns in the center.
From a display of six city cards (or the top of the deck), you draw one or two cards each turn, add one or two to your route, and score for it if you're ready to score. The fact that you *must* add at least one city to your route each turn or lose the whole route gives the game an enjoyable planning element.

RATING: 7
10/2012:7
At first blush, after reading the rules, this game sounded simple, almost boring. The route connection mechanism and also the scoring methods were so, oh ho-hum.After designing Puerto Rico, you would think Seyfarth would top his previous game by designing an even more unique game. After two plays in a 2 player setting, I have to say that there is more to this game than meets the eye. It is most definitely not a hidden gem or a blow-me-over sort of game. However, it is a beautifully layered Euro, that even though is not overly complicated, gives you the usual gamut of head-aching decisions to make. The crux of the game lies in the several ways to end the game and how to maximize your scores. Each has its strengths and weaknesses. Ending the game with the 7-carriage is not as easy as it looks, even with the help of the cartwright. Finishing all the houses appear easier, but will yield you less points if you don't have the carriages to complement your scoring. A good but not great game. It is more complicated than TTR as a gateway game and certainly, I feel it deserves more credit than it has gotten from the standard BGG crowd.

101512: Feel exactly the same way as my previous review. Not the heavy weight as Goa, but clearly not terrible as the initial response. Would introduce this as a gateway game to folks on par with TTR. The balance between building shorter routes and competing for regional tiles to end the game vs. setting up longer routes and getting bonus tiles plus carriages is delicate and quite tight. A good two player experience. Bump to 7 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5

RATING: 8
A challenging game of maximizing each route built. Each route needs to accomplish multiple goals: earn the next carriage level, strategically locate post-offices to eventually claim position bonuses, and (at 5 or more cards) claim route length bonuses. Players may get away with an inefficient route or two, but probably not much more than that. Game ends when a player claims the level 7 (route length 7) carriage or places all post-offices. Sometimes it makes more sense to cash short routes to play your last post offices, than to try to build that Level 7 carriage.

Excellent game - incredibly simple (15 min) to set up and learn - DELICIOUS CHOICES!

RATING: N/A
In Thurn & Taxis, players build post office routes across Bavaria and the regions around, collecting bonus points in various ways. The board shows a map of all the towns, with roads leading from each one to some of its neighbors. There are various colored regions around the board, most with one or two towns, and a large region with all the Bavarian towns in the center.
\13\\13\
From a display of six city cards (or the top of the deck), you draw one or two cards each turn, add one or two to your route, and score for it if you're ready to score. The fact that you *must* add at least one city to your route each turn or lose the whole route gives the game an enjoyable planning element.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Thurn and Taxis feels a lot like Ticket to Ride, but with substantially deeper gameplay. You still collect routes and you still try to claim bonuses for linking different parts of the map. T&T just creates a lot more competition for those routes and the rules for laying down connections leave little room for error. If you start a route and can't add to it every turn until completion, you lose all of your progress and have to start again. It adds a lot of pressure and intensity to every decision, usually the hallmark of a great game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
This was one of the first games I bought, and I loved it at first. However, after about my 5th play, I developed a strategy that I'm pretty sure is optimal, and I played half a dozen more times and won handily each time but once (in which someone else did the same thing I was doing, but quicker). I read somewhere in the forums that many view this as sort of a race game; that may be so, but I don't enjoy that aspect of it. The inability to directly interact with other players also bothers me; after playing Ticket to Ride, I think that game is what I wanted this game to be.

In retrospect, this was the game that snapped me out of "collector" mode and slowed down my game acquisitions, so in that sense, I'm grateful.

RATING: 7
Cute game that evokes Ticket to Ride.  Scoring is completely different though - it's a low scoring game,  although I just realised that everyone actually starts at -20 points.  I think I've got a much better sense of what things are worth now - last game went for extreme carriage action and eked out a win by a single point.   Doesn't appear to have very much player interaction,  but it always seems that the cards you want are swiped by preceding players.  Cards are good quality, and the little houses are nice. I like the pictures on the board,  but the subtle shades of green and red aren't a distinct as I'd like.  I don't think anyone's ever made mistakes with the colours,  so maybe I'm just whining for the sake of it.  Or maybe it's because I've only seen it taught by Rick,  who is my game-teaching idol.

RATING: 8
An unintuitive gameplay makes the game way harder to understand and play efficiently for non-gamers or beginners than its cousin Ticket to Ride. However, it's a great gateway+ game (mind you, don't play it as a next game after Ticket to Ride cause you might get disappointed after trying to compare these 2 totally different games based on the similar mechanic - connecting cities - which is yet so different at its core).
The board is absolutely gorgeous though it can be a little convoluted and hard to grasp once it gets covered with people's houses.
The theme and production values are strong in this one.
A very solid and light title. Highly, highly recommended.
Despite its age, and the trouble of finding a good company willing to play this title over the others, this is a keeper for me.

RATING: 6
Sure, it's much better than Ticket to Ride, but it still left me empty. Using Germany as the map kept spatial relations difficult to determine, especially once the board started filling up with houses. Luck still plays a large part -- perhaps determining the outcome. If I need to purge the draw cards to get 1 card I need while the player to my left happens to get 2 cards he needs at a time, until he can play 2 cards at a time, I'm going to suffer. Especially since there is no way to "catch up" in the game. The game discourages falling behind by having everyone coming in late to a region scoring progressively fewer points. One small spell of bad luck early in the game feels like it would result in an unrecoverable position.

RATING: 7
I've only played this on BSW, which has a really nice interface.  Honestly when I read the rules I wasn't very impressed by Thurn and Taxis, it felt very simplistic and it totally dropped off my radar after I had contemplated on purchasing it.  Anyway, on a whim I decided to give this a shot and was genuinely surprised at how much fun I had with it.  True, the game was no more than collecting the right city cards to build your route, and there is very little strategy involved, it is mostly dependent on whether your opponent is trying to end the game as quickly as possible or prolonging it, so you will need to adjust your style accordingly.  Even so, I've came to appreciate the simpicity rather than my initial disdain of it.

Update: T&T seem to require some defensive plays in drawing cards your opponents need (mostly the leader), this is especially relevant with 3-4 players, and it suffers if people don't realize this.

RATING: 7
Although it is similar to the Ticket to Ride series of games, I felt it had more decision-making and more strategic depth.

The fact that you can see what other players are planning (due to the region bonuses) is a lot more interesting than the hidden agendas of the destination tickets in TtR.

It was about as easy to teach to my family, too, and cheaper to buy!

Would definitely recommend as a family game.
